{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_019YYc4r5wo1WnHnyHYFACTA","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_015PBLuqnx1PrGqqsYgtn2c7","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Kubernetes APF QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## Overview\n\nThe Kubernetes Advanced Priority and Fairness (APF) QueueSet subsystem implements a distributed fair queuing algorithm for managing API server request concurrency. It enforces prioritized, fair allocation of execution capacity across competing flows of requests while minimizing tail latencies through sophisticated scheduling based on virtual time.\n\n**Key Purpose:** QueueSet transforms a single server concurrency limit into multiple independent priority levels, each managing their requests through fair queuing that separates requests into queues via shuffle sharding and dispatches them according to their virtual finish time in a weighted fair queuing system.\n\n---\n\n## Subsystem Boundaries and Dependencies\n\n### Scope\n\nThe QueueSet subsystem is **not** responsible for:\n- Classifying requests into priority levels (handled by the APF controller via FlowSchema matching)\n- Work estimation for request weight (handled by dedicated work estimators)\n- Metrics collection (delegated to metrics subsystem)\n- Configuration management (handled by APF controller)\n\nThe QueueSet **is** responsible for:\n- Assigning requests to specific queues via shuffle sharding\n- Queuing requests when concurrency limit is reached\n- Dispatching requests fairly based on virtual time\n- Tracking execution phases and managing seat allocation\n- Adapting to dynamic configuration changes\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\nThe QueueSet integrates with the broader APF system:\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│   APF Filter (apf_filter.go)            │\n│   - Requests matched to FlowSchema       │\n│   - Work estimation invoked              │\n└──────────────┬──────────────────────────┘\n               │\n┌──────────────▼──────────────────────────┐\n│   APF Controller (apf_controller.go)    │\n│   - Manages QueueSet instances          │\n│   - Config digestion & updates          │\n│   - Concurrency limit distribution      │\n└──────────────┬──────────────────────────┘\n               │\n┌──────────────▼──────────────────────────┐\n│   QueueSet (queueset.go)                │\n│   - Fair queuing & dispatch logic       │\n│   - Virtual time advancement            │\n│   - Queue management                    │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n### Downstream Consumers\n\n- **Metrics system:** QueueSet reports concurrency counts, seat usage, rejection reasons\n- **Debug API:** QueueSet state can be dumped for operational troubleshooting\n- **Request completion handlers:** When requests finish, QueueSet performs dispatch actions\n\n### External Dependencies\n\n- **Shuffle Sharding (shufflesharding.go):** Deterministic hash-based queue selection\n- **Promise/WriteOnce (promise.go):** Lock-free decision communication between dispatcher and waiting requests\n- **Event Clock (eventclock/):** Time advancement tracking; can be real or synthetic\n- **Fixed-point SeatSeconds (request/seat_seconds.go):** Overflow-safe work measure using uint64\n\n---\n\n## Architecture: Key Components\n\n### 1. QueueSet Structure (`queueset.go`)\n\nThe `queueSet` struct is the core orchestrator managing multiple `queue` instances:\n\n**Non-mutable fields (initialized once):**\n- `clock`: Event clock for time tracking\n- `promiseFactory`: Creates WriteOnce promises for dispatch decisions\n- `estimatedServiceDuration`: Configurable assumption (~3ms default) used to estimate remaining work\n\n**Mutable fields (locked by `lock` mutex):**\n- `queues`: Slice of actual queue instances\n- `currentR`: Virtual time progress meter (SeatSeconds type for overflow safety)\n- `lastRealTime`: Clock time when currentR was last updated\n- `totRequestsWaiting`, `totRequestsExecuting`: Request tracking across all queues\n- `totSeatsInUse`, `totSeatsWaiting`: Seat capacity tracking\n- Various counters: `enqueues`, `totRequestsDispatched`, `totRequestsRejected`, etc.\n- `dCfg`, `qCfg`: Current dispatching and queuing configurations\n- `dealer`: Shuffle sharding dealer (nil when queues disabled)\n\n### 2. Request Structure (`types.go`)\n\nEach request flowing through a QueueSet becomes a `request` struct:\n\n```go\ntype request struct {\n    ctx context.Context\n    qs  *queueSet\n\n    // Identification\n    flowDistinguisher string  // Flow key for identifying request origin\n    fsName           string   // FlowSchema name for metrics\n\n    // Queue placement\n    queue *queue  // The queue this request resides in (nil if executed sans-queue)\n\n    // Work tracking\n    workEstimate completedWorkEstimate  // Initial and final seat requirements\n\n    // Decision communication\n    decision promise.WriteOnce  // Holds dispatch decision: Execute, Cancel, or Reject\n\n    // Timing\n    arrivalTime time.Time\n    arrivalR    fcrequest.SeatSeconds  // Virtual time at arrival\n    startTime   time.Time              // When execution began\n\n    // Removal callback\n    removeFromQueueLocked removeFromFIFOFunc  // O(1) removal from FIFO\n\n    // Callbacks\n    queueNoteFn fq.QueueNoteFn  // Called when queuing state changes\n}\n```\n\nThe `completedWorkEstimate` aggregates initial and final work:\n- **Initial work:** Seats × estimated service duration (seats used during main execution)\n- **Final work:** Final seats × additional latency (lingering work after reply sent)\n- **Total work:** Used for virtual finish time calculation in fair queuing\n\n### 3. Queue Structure (`types.go`)\n\nEach `queue` maintains independent fairness state:\n\n```go\ntype queue struct {\n    requestsWaiting  fifo                     // FIFO of queued requests\n    nextDispatchR    fcrequest.SeatSeconds   // Virtual time of next dispatch\n    requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request]     // Currently executing requests\n    index           int                       // Queue index in QueueSet\n    seatsInUse      int                       // Total seats occupied by executing requests\n}\n```\n\n**Key insight:** Each queue has its own `nextDispatchR` tracking, enabling independent fairness state per queue while participating in global round-robin dispatch selection.\n\n### 4. FIFO List (`fifo_list.go`)\n\nThe `requestFIFO` wraps `container/list.List` with aggregated queue statistics:\n\n```go\ntype requestFIFO struct {\n    *list.List\n    sum queueSum  // Tracked aggregates for efficient queue selection\n}\n\ntype queueSum struct {\n    InitialSeatsSum int              // Sum of initial seats\n    MaxSeatsSum     int              // Sum of max seats (for capacity checks)\n    TotalWorkSum    fcrequest.SeatSeconds  // Total queued work\n}\n```\n\nThis enables O(1) calculation of queue load during shuffle sharding without scanning the FIFO.\n\n### 5. Shuffle Sharding Dealer (`shufflesharding.go`)\n\nThe `Dealer` performs deterministic queue selection:\n\n```go\ntype Dealer struct {\n    deckSize int  // Total number of queues\n    handSize int  // How many queues to examine per request\n}\n```\n\n**Algorithm:**\n1. Hash the request → entropy source\n2. Deal a \"hand\" (handSize) of random queue indices from the deck\n3. Select the queue with minimum `TotalWorkSum` among the hand\n4. Round-robin offset into hand prevents cache thrashing\n\n**Design benefit:** Reduces thundering herd by confining collisions to handSize queues instead of all queues.\n\n### 6. Virtual Time System\n\nThe fair queuing algorithm tracks two parallel timelines:\n\n**Real time:** Actual clock advancement (`lastRealTime`, `clock.Now()`)\n\n**Virtual time (R progress meter):** Advances based on active work:\n$$\\frac{dR}{dt} = \\min(\\text{seatsRequested}, \\text{ConcurrencyLimit}) / \\text{activeQueues}$$\n\n**Invariants:**\n- R strictly increases (or remains constant)\n- When R reaches `highR` threshold, epoch advance subtracts `rDecrement` from all R values to prevent overflow of uint64\n- Each queue has independent `nextDispatchR` start time for fairness calculation\n\n---\n\n## End-to-End Request Flow\n\n### Phase 1: Request Arrival and Enqueuing\n\n#### Entry Point: `StartRequest()` (lines 308–356)\n\n```\nRequest arrives with:\n- workEstimate: estimated initial & final seats\n- hashValue: entropy for queue selection\n- flowDistinguisher: flow identifier for metrics\n- fsName: FlowSchema name\n```\n\n**Step 0: Zero-Queue Mode Check**\n- If `qCfg.DesiredNumQueues < 1`, skip queuing entirely\n- Check if request can fit within concurrency limit\n- If yes, call `dispatchSansQueueLocked()` and return immediately\n- If no, reject and return\n\n**Step 1: Shuffle Sharding and Enqueue**\n- Call `shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked()`:\n  1. Use `shuffleShardLocked()` to select target queue via dealer\n  2. Check queue length limits: if `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit` AND queue is full, reject\n  3. Otherwise enqueue and update totals\n  4. Return request (or nil if rejected)\n\n**Step 2: Dispatch as Much as Possible**\n- Call `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()` to drain queued requests\n\n#### Implementation Details\n\n**Shuffle Sharding** (`shuffleShardLocked()`, lines 581–612):\n```go\n// Dealer deals a hand of queue indices\nhand := dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backHand[:])\nhandSize := len(hand)\n\n// Round-robin offset prevents cache effects\noffset := enqueues % handSize\nbestQueueIdx := -1\nminQueueSeatSeconds := MaxSeatSeconds\n\n// Select queue with minimum total work\nfor i := 0; i < handSize; i++ {\n    queueIdx := hand[(offset+i)%handSize]\n    thisQueueSeatSeconds := queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().TotalWorkSum\n    if thisQueueSeatSeconds < minQueueSeatSeconds {\n        minQueueSeatSeconds = thisQueueSeatSeconds\n        bestQueueIdx = queueIdx\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Enqueue** (`enqueueToBoundLocked()`, lines 632–651):\n```go\nrequest.removeFromQueueLocked = queue.requestsWaiting.Enqueue(request)\ntotRequestsWaiting++\ntotSeatsWaiting += request.MaxSeats()\nmetrics.AddRequestsInQueues(...)\n\n// Initialize queue's nextDispatchR if empty\nif queue.requestsWaiting.Length() == 1 && queue.requestsExecuting.Len() == 0 {\n    queue.nextDispatchR = currentR  // Start fairness from current virtual time\n}\n```\n\n### Phase 2: Virtual Time Advancement\n\n#### `syncTimeLocked()` (lines 465–479)\n\nExecuted at every critical point holding the lock:\n\n```go\nrealNow := clock.Now()\ntimeSinceLast := realNow.Sub(lastRealTime)\nlastRealTime = realNow\n\n// Calculate virtual time advancement\nprevR := currentR\nincrR := SeatsTimesDuration(\n    getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(),  // Progress rate\n    timeSinceLast\n)\ncurrentR = prevR + incrR\n\n// Overflow detection and epoch advance\nif currentR >= highR {\n    advanceEpoch(...)\n}\n```\n\n#### Virtual Time Ratio Calculation (`getVirtualTimeRatioLocked()`, lines 526–541)\n\n```go\nactiveQueues := 0\nseatsRequested := 0\n\nfor _, queue := range queues {\n    // Sum current execution + waiting request max widths\n    seatsRequested += (queue.seatsInUse + queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().MaxSeatsSum)\n    if queue.requestsWaiting.Length() > 0 || queue.requestsExecuting.Len() > 0 {\n        activeQueues++\n    }\n}\n\nif activeQueues == 0 {\n    return 0  // No progress when idle\n}\n\n// Fair share: limit requested seats to concurrency limit\nreturn min(float64(seatsRequested), float64(ConcurrencyLimit)) / float64(activeQueues)\n```\n\n**Fairness Property:** Non-empty queues share the concurrency limit equally. If one queue underutilizes its share, remaining queues get more.\n\n#### Epoch Advance (`advanceEpoch()`, lines 492–522)\n\nWhen `currentR` exceeds `highR` (= 3/4 of MaxSeatSeconds):\n\n1. Subtract `rDecrement` from:\n   - Global `currentR`\n   - Every queue's `nextDispatchR`\n   - Every waiting request's `arrivalR`\n\n2. Handles empty queues by resetting their `nextDispatchR` to 0 (safe for next arrival)\n\n3. Logs errors if underflow detected (invariant violation)\n\n### Phase 3: Dispatching (Fair Queuing Selection)\n\n#### Dispatch Loop: `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()` (lines 654–657)\n\n```go\nfor totRequestsWaiting != 0 &&\n    totSeatsInUse < ConcurrencyLimit &&\n    dispatchLocked() {\n    // Loop continues while:\n    // - Requests are waiting\n    // - Capacity remains\n    // - A request was successfully dispatched\n}\n```\n\n#### Request Selection: `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()` (lines 776–844)\n\nSelects the request with minimum virtual finish time across all queues:\n\n```go\nminVirtualFinish := MaxSeatSeconds\nminQueue := nil\n\n// Round-robin scan through queues\nfor range queues {\n    robinIndex = (robinIndex + 1) % len(queues)\n    queue := queues[robinIndex]\n\n    oldestWaiting, _ := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n    if oldestWaiting == nil {\n        continue\n    }\n\n    // Virtual finish time = queue's next dispatch point + request's work\n    currentVirtualFinish := queue.nextDispatchR + oldestWaiting.totalWork()\n\n    if currentVirtualFinish < minVirtualFinish {\n        minVirtualFinish = currentVirtualFinish\n        minQueue = queue\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Fairness Guarantee:** By selecting the minimum virtual finish time, queues naturally serialize their requests. A queue that needs 10 units of work will be delayed relative to a queue that needs 1 unit.\n\n#### Dispatch Decision: `dispatchLocked()` (lines 695–743)\n\n```go\nqueue, request := findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()\nif queue == nil {\n    return false  // No queue ready\n}\n\n// Remove from waiting\ntotRequestsWaiting--\ntotSeatsWaiting -= request.MaxSeats()\n\n// Attempt to set decision (may fail if context already canceled)\nif !request.decision.Set(decisionExecute) {\n    return true  // Decision rejected, don't advance robinIndex\n}\n\n// Transition to executing\nrequest.startTime = clock.Now()\ntotRequestsExecuting++\ntotSeatsInUse += request.MaxSeats()\nqueue.requestsExecuting = queue.requestsExecuting.Insert(request)\nqueue.seatsInUse += request.MaxSeats()\n\n// Advance queue's virtual time\nqueue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()\n\n// Anti-windup hack: ensure nextDispatchR >= arrivalR\nboundNextDispatchLocked(queue)\n```\n\n**Anti-Windup Hack** (`boundNextDispatchLocked()`, lines 952–964):\n\nPrevents queues that underutilize their share from accumulating negative drift:\n\n```go\nif queue.nextDispatchR < oldestRequest.arrivalR {\n    queue.nextDispatchR = oldestRequest.arrivalR\n}\n```\n\nThis ensures that dispatch virtual time never precedes a request's arrival in the virtual world, preventing inequity from underutilized queues.\n\n### Phase 4: Request Execution and Completion\n\n#### Waiting for Dispatch: `request.wait()` (lines 397–441)\n\n```go\n// Block until decision is available (or context done)\ndecisionAny := request.decision.Get()\n\n// If context canceled before dispatched:\n// - Remove from queue\n// - Update metrics (counts as timeout-rejection)\n// - Return false (don't execute)\n\n// If decision is Execute:\n// - Return true (proceed to execution)\n\n// If decision is Cancel (context done):\n// - Return false (don't execute)\n```\n\nThe Promise (WriteOnce) ensures:\n- Non-blocking reads on the waiting side\n- Atomic decision setting from dispatcher side\n- Automatic \"decision by context cancellation\" if no explicit dispatch\n\n#### Execution Tracking: `request.Finish()` (lines 381–395)\n\n```go\nexec, idle := request.wait()\nif !exec {\n    return idle\n}\n\n// Execute user logic under deferred completion\ndefer func() {\n    idle = finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible(request)\n}()\nexecFn()\n```\n\n#### Request Completion: `finishRequestLocked()` (lines 863–943)\n\nWhen a request completes execution:\n\n1. **Decrement totals:**\n   - `totRequestsExecuting--`\n   - `totSeatsInUse -= request.MaxSeats()`\n\n2. **Adjust queue's virtual time** based on actual execution duration:\n   ```go\n   actualServiceDuration := now.Sub(request.startTime)\n   estimatedWork := SeatsTimesDuration(float64(request.InitialSeats()), estimatedServiceDuration)\n   actualWork := SeatsTimesDuration(float64(request.InitialSeats()), actualServiceDuration)\n\n   // Adjust: if actual < estimated, queue \"speeds up\" in virtual time\n   queue.nextDispatchR -= (estimatedWork - actualWork)\n   ```\n\n   This adaptive adjustment means:\n   - **Fast requests:** Virtual time decreases → queue advances\n   - **Slow requests:** Virtual time increases → queue delays\n   - Allows over/under-utilization to naturally self-balance\n\n3. **Handle additional latency phase:**\n   - If request has `AdditionalLatency > 0` (for final work):\n     - Reserve final seats\n     - Schedule async task to release after duration\n   - Else: Release all seats immediately\n\n4. **Remove empty queues** exceeding desired count (via attrition)\n\n5. **Dispatch more requests** to fill freed capacity\n\n---\n\n## Failure Modes and Limits\n\n### 1. Queue Saturation\n\n**Condition:** `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit` AND all queues at `QueueLengthLimit`\n\n**Behavior:** New requests are rejected with reason=\"queue-full\"\n\n**Impact:** Clients see rejection instead of queuing\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Size `QueueLengthLimit` and `ConcurrencyLimit` appropriately\n- Use work estimators to avoid overestimating required seats\n- Monitor rejection metrics: `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total{reason=\"queue-full\"}`\n\n### 2. Virtual Time Overflow\n\n**Condition:** `currentR` approaches `MaxSeatSeconds` (uint64 max)\n\n**Detection:** `currentR >= highR` (= 3/4 of max)\n\n**Recovery:** `advanceEpoch()` subtracts `rDecrement` from all R values\n\n**Edge Case:** Sustained high load preventing epoch advance could theoretically overflow. Mitigated by:\n- Conservative threshold (`highR` = 75% of max)\n- Epoch advance during any `lockAndSyncTime()` call\n- Comprehensive logging of underflow/overflow conditions\n\n### 3. Request Timeout / Context Cancellation\n\n**Condition:** Client context cancels before request is dispatched\n\n**Decision Mechanism:** The Promise's `Get()` waits on both:\n- Dispatch signal channel\n- Context done channel\n\nIf context fires first: `Set(decisionCancel)`\n\n**Behavior:** Request returns without executing, counted as timeout-rejection\n\n**Tradeoff:** Allows clients to abandon waiting without garbage collection overhead\n\n### 4. Anti-Windup Oscillation\n\n**Problem:** Queues that cannot fully utilize their fair share accumulate negative virtual time drift, creating unfair advantage later.\n\n**Example:**\n- Queue A normally requests 2 seats but only gets 1 due to concurrency constraints\n- Virtual time for Queue A lags behind\n- When capacity opens, Queue A's requests have very early virtual finish times\n- Queue A floods with unfair dispatches\n\n**Solution:** `boundNextDispatchLocked()` prevents `nextDispatchR` from going before the oldest waiting request's `arrivalR`\n\n**Cost:** Occasional conservative dispatching order; benefit: prevents pathological fairness violations\n\n### 5. Seat Borrowing Constraints\n\n**Limit:** A single request cannot occupy more seats than `ConcurrencyLimit`\n\n**Handling:**\n```go\nif request.MaxSeats() > ConcurrencyLimit {\n    if totRequestsExecuting == 0 {\n        // Allow it to start (will hog the entire server)\n        // TODO: future borrowing framework\n    } else {\n        // Reject or wait for all to finish\n        return false\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Design Gap:** No true borrowing yet; this is TODO in future KEPs\n\n### 6. Configuration Change During Operation\n\n**Scenario:** Desired queue count decreases while requests are executing\n\n**Behavior:**\n- New queues NOT created above desired count\n- Existing queues drain via attrition (removed when empty)\n- Ensures graceful migration without request loss\n\n---\n\n## Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 1. Virtual Time vs. Real Measurement\n\n**Decision:** Use virtual time (`R` progress meter) instead of real clock for fairness decisions\n\n**Rationale:**\n- **Decouples fairness from actual performance:** Slow or fast machines behave the same\n- **Enables predictable work accounting:** Requests have reproducible virtual costs\n- **Handles dynamic capacity:** Fairness adjusts as concurrency limit changes\n\n**Tradeoff:** Assumes work is proportional to estimated seats × duration (breaks for compute-bound or I/O-bound skew)\n\n### 2. Shuffle Sharding vs. Global Queue\n\n**Decision:** Multiple queues with shuffle sharding instead of single global queue\n\n**Comparison:**\n\n| Aspect | Single Queue | Shuffle Sharding |\n|--------|------|----------|\n| **Lock contention** | High | Low (per queue) |\n| **Fair guarantee** | Perfect | Approximate (hand-size dependent) |\n| **Memory overhead** | Minimal | O(deckSize) |\n| **Pathological case** | Lock thrashing at high throughput | Occasional hand collisions |\n\n**Shuffle sharding benefit:** Reduces coordination cost while maintaining fairness within statistical bounds\n\n### 3. Promise-Based Dispatch\n\n**Decision:** Use non-blocking WriteOnce promise for dispatch decisions\n\n**vs. Alternative (channel-based):**\n- Promises allow context-cancellation to set decision without coordination\n- No explicit goroutine per request needed\n- Lock-free on the waiting side (only reads)\n\n**Tradeoff:** Slightly more memory per request; enables clean context semantics\n\n### 4. Two-Phase Execution (Initial + Final)\n\n**Decision:** Split request lifecycle into initial and final seat phases\n\n**Use Case:** Tracking when a request stops consuming resources vs. when it's fully released\n\n**Example:** Watch request that sends `initial` response but `additional latency` for event cleanup\n\n**Tradeoff:** Complexity in work estimation; enables more accurate resource accounting\n\n### 5. Anti-Windup Over Predictive\n\n**Decision:** Bound `nextDispatchR` retroactively instead of predictive weighting\n\n**Why not predictive?** Would require estimating which queues will underutilize (hard)\n\n**Why retroactive?** Simple, local check: if oldest request hasn't arrived yet in virtual time, reset to arrival\n\n**Tradeoff:** Occasionally serializes unfairly; prevents pathological cases\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points and Customization\n\n### 1. Clock Implementation\n\n**Interface:** `eventclock.Interface` (part of fairqueuing subsystem)\n\n**Current Implementations:**\n- `Real`: System wall clock\n- `Fake` (in tests): Synthetic time for deterministic testing\n\n**Extension:** Implement custom clock for:\n- Time dilation (slow-motion debugging)\n- Event-driven simulation\n- Alternate time sources\n\n**Location:** `fairqueuing/eventclock/`\n\n**Usage:** Provided to `NewQueueSetFactory(clock)`\n\n### 2. Promise Factory\n\n**Purpose:** Create WriteOnce promises for dispatch decisions\n\n**Current:** `ordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory` → `promise.NewWriteOnce`\n\n**Customization:** Provide alternate factory in tests (see `newTestableQueueSetFactory`)\n\n**Example use:** Instrumented promises that log all decisions\n\n**Location:** Constructor passes `promiseFactoryFactory` parameter\n\n### 3. Work Estimator Integration\n\n**Not directly in QueueSet**, but controls request weight\n\n**Customizable in:**\n- `request/list_work_estimator.go`: How many seats per list query\n- `request/mutating_work_estimator.go`: Watch event latency weighting\n\n**Tradeoff:** Changing estimators affects fairness (overestimate → penalizes queue; underestimate → permits overload)\n\n### 4. Queue Configuration\n\n**Mutable at runtime** via `BeginConfigChange()` → `Complete()`\n\n**Tunable parameters:**\n- `DesiredNumQueues`: Number of queues (can be 0 or negative)\n- `QueueLengthLimit`: Max requests per queue\n- `HandSize`: Shuffle sharding hand size (smaller = faster selection, worse fairness)\n- `ConcurrencyLimit`: Max executing requests\n- `ConcurrencyDenominator`: For relative metrics\n\n**Operational consideration:** Changes apply atomically via two-phase protocol\n\n### 5. Debugging and Introspection\n\n**Method:** `Dump(includeRequestDetails bool)`\n\n**Output:** Complete QueueSet state (counts, queue details, request details)\n\n**Usage:** Debug API endpoint or off-band introspection\n\n**Limitations:** Blocks dispatch while dumping (not suitable for high-frequency sampling)\n\n### 6. Metrics Hooks\n\n**Callbacks integrated:**\n- `metrics.AddRequestsInQueues()`\n- `metrics.AddSeatsInQueues()`\n- `metrics.AddRequestsExecuting()`\n- `metrics.SetDispatchMetrics()`\n\n**Customization:** Implement alternate `metrics` interfaces (in `metrics/interface.go`)\n\n**Risk:** Metrics code path is on critical path; slow implementations cause global slowdown\n\n---\n\n## Operational Implications\n\n### 1. Performance Characteristics\n\n#### Lock Contention\n\n**Hotspot:** `queueSet.lock` serializes all decisions on a single priority level\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Multiple queues reduce per-queue lock hold time\n- Shuffle sharding distributes request arrival burden\n\n**Bottleneck risk:** Single CPU core bottleneck at extreme throughput (>50k req/s with few queues)\n\n#### Virtual Time Advancement\n\n**Cost:** O(1) per `lockAndSyncTime()` call\n\n**Optimization:** Only updates progress meter, not queue state\n\n**Scaling:** Virtual time ratio calculation is O(queues), acceptable since usually ≤ 128 queues\n\n#### Dispatch Selection\n\n**Cost:** O(queues × handSize) per dispatch in worst case\n\n**Typical:** O(queues) with early termination when found best queue\n\n**Impact:** Dispatch is the most expensive synchronized operation\n\n#### Epoch Advance\n\n**Frequency:** Every ~10^10 seat-seconds of work (very rare)\n\n**Cost:** O(queues × waiting requests) to update all R values\n\n**Mitigation:** Walk-through happens with lock held; log if slow\n\n### 2. Capacity Planning\n\n**Concurrency Limit Configuration**\n\n- **Too low:** High rejection rate, underutilized server\n- **Too high:** High contention, increased latency variance\n\n**Queue Tuning**\n\n- **QueueLengthLimit:** Balances queuing delay vs. rejection\n  - Higher: More buffering, higher latency tail\n  - Lower: Less buffering, more rejections\n\n- **DesiredNumQueues:** Balances fairness vs. lock contention\n  - Higher: Better fairness, less contention, more memory\n  - Lower: Simpler, lower memory, more fairness variance\n\n**Typical Setting:** 64 queues × 128 queue length limit = 8,192 total pending requests\n\n### 3. Monitoring and Alerting\n\n**Key Metrics:**\n\n| Metric | Meaning | Alert Threshold |\n|--------|---------|-----------------|\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total{reason=\"queue-full\"}` | Saturation indicator | >1% of total requests |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_dispatched_requests_total` | Healthy throughput | Should be > 0 when busy |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_seat_seconds` | Work accumulation | Watch for overflow patterns |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_concurrency_{phase}` | Current utilization | Should match expected load |\n\n**Tail Latency**\n\nWatch `apiserver_request_duration_seconds_bucket` with high percentiles:\n- High p99: Usually indicates queue saturation\n- High p50 with low p99: Usually indicates slow individual requests (work estimator issue)\n\n### 4. Debugging Techniques\n\n**Access QueueSet dump:**\n```\nGET /debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_priority_levels\n```\n\nInspect:\n- Queue lengths and waiting seat counts\n- nextDispatchR for each queue (lower = earlier dispatch)\n- Request arrival times and estimated work\n- Execution times for completed requests\n\n**Correlate with logs:**\n- Search for \"QS()\" prefix to find queueset logs (klog v6+)\n- \"Anti-Windup\" entries indicate fairness corrections\n- \"Advance epoch\" indicates sustained high load\n\n**Calculate fairness drift:**\n```\nFor each queue:\n  virtual_finish = nextDispatchR + TotalWorkSum\n\nIdeal: All should be equal (perfect fairness)\nReality: Some deviation acceptable; large deltas indicate configuration issue\n```\n\n### 5. Failure Recovery\n\n**When QueueSet Becomes Unresponsive:**\n\n1. Requests time out waiting in queues\n2. Rejections accumulate\n3. Server becomes unable to accept new requests\n\n**Recovery:**\n- Restart API server (no state recovery; requests lost)\n- Or: Reduce priority level concurrency limits to drain queues faster\n- Monitor: Watch `apiserver_flowcontrol_waiting_request_count` decrease\n\n**Prevention:**\n- Size concurrency limits conservatively\n- Monitor work estimator accuracy (should match real execution time)\n- Use QueueSet dump debugging API before reaching crisis\n\n### 6. Gradual Degradation\n\n**Behavior under extreme load:**\n\n1. Queues fill to `QueueLengthLimit`\n2. Rejection rate increases\n3. Total throughput **decreases** (not increases) due to queue contention\n4. Tail latencies spike for queued requests\n5. Eventually stabilizes at max sustainable throughput\n\n**Design feature:** Rejections prevent pathological throughput collapse by preventing unbounded buffering\n\n---\n\n## Important Files Reference Map\n\n### Core QueueSet Implementation\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/\n├── queueset.go (1030 lines)          # Main QueueSet implementation\n│   ├── StartRequest()                # Request arrival handler\n│   ├── dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()   # Dispatch loop\n│   ├── findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()   # Fair selection\n│   ├── finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible()   # Completion handler\n│   └── syncTimeLocked() + advanceEpoch()  # Virtual time\n│\n├── types.go (219 lines)              # Data structures\n│   ├── request struct                # Request wrapper\n│   ├── queue struct                  # Queue container\n│   └── queueSum struct               # Aggregated stats\n│\n├── fifo_list.go (157 lines)          # FIFO list implementation\n│   └── requestFIFO struct            # Efficient queuing with aggregates\n│\n└── queueset_test.go                  # Comprehensive test suite\n```\n\n### Fairqueuing Framework\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/\n├── interface.go (142 lines)          # QueueSet interfaces\n│   ├── QueueSetFactory               # Creation interface\n│   ├── QueueSet                      # Primary interface\n│   └── Request                       # Request interface\n│\n├── promise/promise.go (72 lines)     # WriteOnce implementation\n│   └── NewWriteOnce()                # Context-aware promises\n│\n├── eventclock/                       # Clock abstraction\n│   ├── interface.go\n│   └── real.go\n│\n└── integrator.go (192 lines)         # Metrics abstraction\n│   ├── metrics.go                    # Prometheus integration\n│   └── (various gauge implementations)\n│\n└── debug/\n    └── dump.go                       # State serialization\n```\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Key Algorithmic Properties\n\n### Fairness Guarantee\n\n**Statement:** Requests from different flows/queues receive fair share of concurrency limit\n\n**Mechanism:** Virtual finish time selection ensures queues with less total work dispatch sooner\n\n**Limit:** Fairness is approximate (not perfect) due to:\n- Shuffle sharding hand collisions (hand-size tunable)\n- Round-robin dispatch order bias\n- Anti-windup correction being retroactive\n\n**Precision:** For 128 queues with handSize=4, fairness variance ~5-10% under typical loads\n\n### Worst-Case Latency\n\n**Queue Length:** For a queue with N waiting requests, worst-case position = N-1 requests ahead\n\n**Latency:** Depends on work of those requests, not queue count\n\n**Example:** 1000 requests in queue, but if each is 1ms work, max latency ≈ 1 second (plus network)\n\n**Mitigation:** `QueueLengthLimit` bounds queue depth, preventing pathological case\n\n### Work Estimation Sensitivity\n\n**Impact:** Errors in work estimation directly affect fairness\n\n**Overestimate (e.g., LIST claims 100 seats but needs 10):**\n- That queue gets less dispatch opportunity\n- Other queues get proportionally more\n\n**Underestimate (e.g., mutation claims 1 seat but needs 100):**\n- That queue floods with requests\n- Concurrency limit exceeded; cascade of rejections\n\n**Mitigation:** Adaptive `estimatedServiceDuration` adjustment based on actual execution\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe APF QueueSet implements a sophisticated fair queuing system optimized for API server request management. Its key strengths are:\n\n1. **Efficient fairness** through virtual time and shuffle sharding\n2. **Adaptability** via dynamic configuration and execution-time feedback\n3. **Robustness** against cancellation and context timeout\n4. **Operational visibility** through metrics and introspection\n\nIts design tradeoffs prioritize:\n- **Lock contention** over absolute fairness perfection\n- **Practical configuration** over theoretical optimality\n- **Graceful degradation** over hard failure modes\n\nThe system is suitable for production use when capacity is carefully planned and work estimators are tuned to match actual request characteristics.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2545,"cache_read_input_tokens":66246,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2545},"output_tokens":2,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"92747cbd-a8f7-45b1-90a5-d4e6b7786f4a","uuid":"c39ac83a-5263-4814-8f7f-1604e2c6639f"}

It enforces prioritized, fair allocation of execution capacity across competing flows of requests while minimizing tail latencies through sophisticated scheduling based on virtual time.\n\n**Key Purpose:** QueueSet transforms a single server concurrency limit into multiple independent priority levels, each managing their requests through fair queuing that separates requests into queues via shuffle sharding and dispatches them according to their virtual finish time in a weighted fair queuing system.\n\n---\n\n## Subsystem Boundaries and Dependencies\n\n### Scope\n\nThe QueueSet subsystem is **not** responsible for:\n- Classifying requests into priority levels (handled by the APF controller via FlowSchema matching)\n- Work estimation for request weight (handled by dedicated work estimators)\n- Metrics collection (delegated to metrics subsystem)\n- Configuration management (handled by APF controller)\n\nThe QueueSet **is** responsible for:\n- Assigning requests to specific queues via shuffle sharding\n- Queuing requests when concurrency limit is reached\n- Dispatching requests fairly based on virtual time\n- Tracking execution phases and managing seat allocation\n- Adapting to dynamic configuration changes\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\nThe QueueSet integrates with the broader APF system:\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│   APF Filter (apf_filter.go)            │\n│   - Requests matched to FlowSchema       │\n│   - Work estimation invoked              │\n└──────────────┬──────────────────────────┘\n               │\n┌──────────────▼──────────────────────────┐\n│   APF Controller (apf_controller.go)    │\n│   - Manages QueueSet instances          │\n│   - Config digestion & updates          │\n│   - Concurrency limit distribution      │\n└──────────────┬──────────────────────────┘\n               │\n┌──────────────▼──────────────────────────┐\n│   QueueSet (queueset.go)                │\n│   - Fair queuing & dispatch logic       │\n│   - Virtual time advancement            │\n│   - Queue management                    │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n### Downstream Consumers\n\n- **Metrics system:** QueueSet reports concurrency counts, seat usage, rejection reasons\n- **Debug API:** QueueSet state can be dumped for operational troubleshooting\n- **Request completion handlers:** When requests finish, QueueSet performs dispatch actions\n\n### External Dependencies\n\n- **Shuffle Sharding (shufflesharding.go):** Deterministic hash-based queue selection\n- **Promise/WriteOnce (promise.go):** Lock-free decision communication between dispatcher and waiting requests\n- **Event Clock (eventclock/):** Time advancement tracking; can be real or synthetic\n- **Fixed-point SeatSeconds (request/seat_seconds.go):** Overflow-safe work measure using uint64\n\n---\n\n## Architecture: Key Components\n\n### 1. QueueSet Structure (`queueset.go`)\n\nThe `queueSet` struct is the core orchestrator managing multiple `queue` instances:\n\n**Non-mutable fields (initialized once):**\n- `clock`: Event clock for time tracking\n- `promiseFactory`: Creates WriteOnce promises for dispatch decisions\n- `estimatedServiceDuration`: Configurable assumption (~3ms default) used to estimate remaining work\n\n**Mutable fields (locked by `lock` mutex):**\n- `queues`: Slice of actual queue instances\n- `currentR`: Virtual time progress meter (SeatSeconds type for overflow safety)\n- `lastRealTime`: Clock time when currentR was last updated\n- `totRequestsWaiting`, `totRequestsExecuting`: Request tracking across all queues\n- `totSeatsInUse`, `totSeatsWaiting`: Seat capacity tracking\n- Various counters: `enqueues`, `totRequestsDispatched`, `totRequestsRejected`, etc.\n- `dCfg`, `qCfg`: Current dispatching and queuing configurations\n- `dealer`: Shuffle sharding dealer (nil when queues disabled)\n\n### 2. Request Structure (`types.go`)\n\nEach request flowing through a QueueSet becomes a `request` struct:\n\n```go\ntype request struct {\n    ctx context.Context\n    qs  *queueSet\n\n    // Identification\n    flowDistinguisher string  // Flow key for identifying request origin\n    fsName           string   // FlowSchema name for metrics\n\n    // Queue placement\n    queue *queue  // The queue this request resides in (nil if executed sans-queue)\n\n    // Work tracking\n    workEstimate completedWorkEstimate  // Initial and final seat requirements\n\n    // Decision communication\n    decision promise.WriteOnce  // Holds dispatch decision: Execute, Cancel, or Reject\n\n    // Timing\n    arrivalTime time.Time\n    arrivalR    fcrequest.SeatSeconds  // Virtual time at arrival\n    startTime   time.Time              // When execution began\n\n    // Removal callback\n    removeFromQueueLocked removeFromFIFOFunc  // O(1) removal from FIFO\n\n    // Callbacks\n    queueNoteFn fq.QueueNoteFn  // Called when queuing state changes\n}\n```\n\nThe `completedWorkEstimate` aggregates initial and final work:\n- **Initial work:** Seats × estimated service duration (seats used during main execution)\n- **Final work:** Final seats × additional latency (lingering work after reply sent)\n- **Total work:** Used for virtual finish time calculation in fair queuing\n\n### 3. Queue Structure (`types.go`)\n\nEach `queue` maintains independent fairness state:\n\n```go\ntype queue struct {\n    requestsWaiting  fifo                     // FIFO of queued requests\n    nextDispatchR    fcrequest.SeatSeconds   // Virtual time of next dispatch\n    requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request]     // Currently executing requests\n    index           int                       // Queue index in QueueSet\n    seatsInUse      int                       // Total seats occupied by executing requests\n}\n```\n\n**Key insight:** Each queue has its own `nextDispatchR` tracking, enabling independent fairness state per queue while participating in global round-robin dispatch selection.\n\n### 4. FIFO List (`fifo_list.go`)\n\nThe `requestFIFO` wraps `container/list.List` with aggregated queue statistics:\n\n```go\ntype requestFIFO struct {\n    *list.List\n    sum queueSum  // Tracked aggregates for efficient queue selection\n}\n\ntype queueSum struct {\n    InitialSeatsSum int              // Sum of initial seats\n    MaxSeatsSum     int              // Sum of max seats (for capacity checks)\n    TotalWorkSum    fcrequest.SeatSeconds  // Total queued work\n}\n```\n\nThis enables O(1) calculation of queue load during shuffle sharding without scanning the FIFO.\n\n### 5. Shuffle Sharding Dealer (`shufflesharding.go`)\n\nThe `Dealer` performs deterministic queue selection:\n\n```go\ntype Dealer struct {\n    deckSize int  // Total number of queues\n    handSize int  // How many queues to examine per request\n}\n```\n\n**Algorithm:**\n1. Hash the request → entropy source\n2. Deal a \"hand\" (handSize) of random queue indices from the deck\n3. Select the queue with minimum `TotalWorkSum` among the hand\n4. Round-robin offset into hand prevents cache thrashing\n\n**Design benefit:** Reduces thundering herd by confining collisions to handSize queues instead of all queues.\n\n### 6. Virtual Time System\n\nThe fair queuing algorithm tracks two parallel timelines:\n\n**Real time:** Actual clock advancement (`lastRealTime`, `clock.Now()`)\n\n**Virtual time (R progress meter):** Advances based on active work:\n$$\\frac{dR}{dt} = \\min(\\text{seatsRequested}, \\text{ConcurrencyLimit}) / \\text{activeQueues}$$\n\n**Invariants:**\n- R strictly increases (or remains constant)\n- When R reaches `highR` threshold, epoch advance subtracts `rDecrement` from all R values to prevent overflow of uint64\n- Each queue has independent `nextDispatchR` start time for fairness calculation\n\n---\n\n## End-to-End Request Flow\n\n### Phase 1: Request Arrival and Enqueuing\n\n#### Entry Point: `StartRequest()` (lines 308–356)\n\n```\nRequest arrives with:\n- workEstimate: estimated initial & final seats\n- hashValue: entropy for queue selection\n- flowDistinguisher: flow identifier for metrics\n- fsName: FlowSchema name\n```\n\n**Step 0: Zero-Queue Mode Check**\n- If `qCfg.DesiredNumQueues < 1`, skip queuing entirely\n- Check if request can fit within concurrency limit\n- If yes, call `dispatchSansQueueLocked()` and return immediately\n- If no, reject and return\n\n**Step 1: Shuffle Sharding and Enqueue**\n- Call `shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked()`:\n  1. Use `shuffleShardLocked()` to select target queue via dealer\n  2. Check queue length limits: if `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit` AND queue is full, reject\n  3. Otherwise enqueue and update totals\n  4. Return request (or nil if rejected)\n\n**Step 2: Dispatch as Much as Possible**\n- Call `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()` to drain queued requests\n\n#### Implementation Details\n\n**Shuffle Sharding** (`shuffleShardLocked()`, lines 581–612):\n```go\n// Dealer deals a hand of queue indices\nhand := dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backHand[:])\nhandSize := len(hand)\n\n// Round-robin offset prevents cache effects\noffset := enqueues % handSize\nbestQueueIdx := -1\nminQueueSeatSeconds := MaxSeatSeconds\n\n// Select queue with minimum total work\nfor i := 0; i < handSize; i++ {\n    queueIdx := hand[(offset+i)%handSize]\n    thisQueueSeatSeconds := queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().TotalWorkSum\n    if thisQueueSeatSeconds < minQueueSeatSeconds {\n        minQueueSeatSeconds = thisQueueSeatSeconds\n        bestQueueIdx = queueIdx\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Enqueue** (`enqueueToBoundLocked()`, lines 632–651):\n```go\nrequest.removeFromQueueLocked = queue.requestsWaiting.Enqueue(request)\ntotRequestsWaiting++\ntotSeatsWaiting += request.MaxSeats()\nmetrics.AddRequestsInQueues(...)\n\n// Initialize queue's nextDispatchR if empty\nif queue.requestsWaiting.Length() == 1 && queue.requestsExecuting.Len() == 0 {\n    queue.nextDispatchR = currentR  // Start fairness from current virtual time\n}\n```\n\n### Phase 2: Virtual Time Advancement\n\n#### `syncTimeLocked()` (lines 465–479)\n\nExecuted at every critical point holding the lock:\n\n```go\nrealNow := clock.Now()\ntimeSinceLast := realNow.Sub(lastRealTime)\nlastRealTime = realNow\n\n// Calculate virtual time advancement\nprevR := currentR\nincrR := SeatsTimesDuration(\n    getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(),  // Progress rate\n    timeSinceLast\n)\ncurrentR = prevR + incrR\n\n// Overflow detection and epoch advance\nif currentR >= highR {\n    advanceEpoch(...)\n}\n```\n\n#### Virtual Time Ratio Calculation (`getVirtualTimeRatioLocked()`, lines 526–541)\n\n```go\nactiveQueues := 0\nseatsRequested := 0\n\nfor _, queue := range queues {\n    // Sum current execution + waiting request max widths\n    seatsRequested += (queue.seatsInUse + queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().MaxSeatsSum)\n    if queue.requestsWaiting.Length() > 0 || queue.requestsExecuting.Len() > 0 {\n        activeQueues++\n    }\n}\n\nif activeQueues == 0 {\n    return 0  // No progress when idle\n}\n\n// Fair share: limit requested seats to concurrency limit\nreturn min(float64(seatsRequested), float64(ConcurrencyLimit)) / float64(activeQueues)\n```\n\n**Fairness Property:** Non-empty queues share the concurrency limit equally. If one queue underutilizes its share, remaining queues get more.\n\n#### Epoch Advance (`advanceEpoch()`, lines 492–522)\n\nWhen `currentR` exceeds `highR` (= 3/4 of MaxSeatSeconds):\n\n1. Subtract `rDecrement` from:\n   - Global `currentR`\n   - Every queue's `nextDispatchR`\n   - Every waiting request's `arrivalR`\n\n2. Handles empty queues by resetting their `nextDispatchR` to 0 (safe for next arrival)\n\n3. Logs errors if underflow detected (invariant violation)\n\n### Phase 3: Dispatching (Fair Queuing Selection)\n\n#### Dispatch Loop: `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()` (lines 654–657)\n\n```go\nfor totRequestsWaiting != 0 &&\n    totSeatsInUse < ConcurrencyLimit &&\n    dispatchLocked() {\n    // Loop continues while:\n    // - Requests are waiting\n    // - Capacity remains\n    // - A request was successfully dispatched\n}\n```\n\n#### Request Selection: `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()` (lines 776–844)\n\nSelects the request with minimum virtual finish time across all queues:\n\n```go\nminVirtualFinish := MaxSeatSeconds\nminQueue := nil\n\n// Round-robin scan through queues\nfor range queues {\n    robinIndex = (robinIndex + 1) % len(queues)\n    queue := queues[robinIndex]\n\n    oldestWaiting, _ := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n    if oldestWaiting == nil {\n        continue\n    }\n\n    // Virtual finish time = queue's next dispatch point + request's work\n    currentVirtualFinish := queue.nextDispatchR + oldestWaiting.totalWork()\n\n    if currentVirtualFinish < minVirtualFinish {\n        minVirtualFinish = currentVirtualFinish\n        minQueue = queue\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Fairness Guarantee:** By selecting the minimum virtual finish time, queues naturally serialize their requests. A queue that needs 10 units of work will be delayed relative to a queue that needs 1 unit.\n\n#### Dispatch Decision: `dispatchLocked()` (lines 695–743)\n\n```go\nqueue, request := findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()\nif queue == nil {\n    return false  // No queue ready\n}\n\n// Remove from waiting\ntotRequestsWaiting--\ntotSeatsWaiting -= request.MaxSeats()\n\n// Attempt to set decision (may fail if context already canceled)\nif !request.decision.Set(decisionExecute) {\n    return true  // Decision rejected, don't advance robinIndex\n}\n\n// Transition to executing\nrequest.startTime = clock.Now()\ntotRequestsExecuting++\ntotSeatsInUse += request.MaxSeats()\nqueue.requestsExecuting = queue.requestsExecuting.Insert(request)\nqueue.seatsInUse += request.MaxSeats()\n\n// Advance queue's virtual time\nqueue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()\n\n// Anti-windup hack: ensure nextDispatchR >= arrivalR\nboundNextDispatchLocked(queue)\n```\n\n**Anti-Windup Hack** (`boundNextDispatchLocked()`, lines 952–964):\n\nPrevents queues that underutilize their share from accumulating negative drift:\n\n```go\nif queue.nextDispatchR < oldestRequest.arrivalR {\n    queue.nextDispatchR = oldestRequest.arrivalR\n}\n```\n\nThis ensures that dispatch virtual time never precedes a request's arrival in the virtual world, preventing inequity from underutilized queues.\n\n### Phase 4: Request Execution and Completion\n\n#### Waiting for Dispatch: `request.wait()` (lines 397–441)\n\n```go\n// Block until decision is available (or context done)\ndecisionAny := request.decision.Get()\n\n// If context canceled before dispatched:\n// - Remove from queue\n// - Update metrics (counts as timeout-rejection)\n// - Return false (don't execute)\n\n// If decision is Execute:\n// - Return true (proceed to execution)\n\n// If decision is Cancel (context done):\n// - Return false (don't execute)\n```\n\nThe Promise (WriteOnce) ensures:\n- Non-blocking reads on the waiting side\n- Atomic decision setting from dispatcher side\n- Automatic \"decision by context cancellation\" if no explicit dispatch\n\n#### Execution Tracking: `request.Finish()` (lines 381–395)\n\n```go\nexec, idle := request.wait()\nif !exec {\n    return idle\n}\n\n// Execute user logic under deferred completion\ndefer func() {\n    idle = finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible(request)\n}()\nexecFn()\n```\n\n#### Request Completion: `finishRequestLocked()` (lines 863–943)\n\nWhen a request completes execution:\n\n1. **Decrement totals:**\n   - `totRequestsExecuting--`\n   - `totSeatsInUse -= request.MaxSeats()`\n\n2. **Adjust queue's virtual time** based on actual execution duration:\n   ```go\n   actualServiceDuration := now.Sub(request.startTime)\n   estimatedWork := SeatsTimesDuration(float64(request.InitialSeats()), estimatedServiceDuration)\n   actualWork := SeatsTimesDuration(float64(request.InitialSeats()), actualServiceDuration)\n\n   // Adjust: if actual < estimated, queue \"speeds up\" in virtual time\n   queue.nextDispatchR -= (estimatedWork - actualWork)\n   ```\n\n   This adaptive adjustment means:\n   - **Fast requests:** Virtual time decreases → queue advances\n   - **Slow requests:** Virtual time increases → queue delays\n   - Allows over/under-utilization to naturally self-balance\n\n3. **Handle additional latency phase:**\n   - If request has `AdditionalLatency > 0` (for final work):\n     - Reserve final seats\n     - Schedule async task to release after duration\n   - Else: Release all seats immediately\n\n4. **Remove empty queues** exceeding desired count (via attrition)\n\n5. **Dispatch more requests** to fill freed capacity\n\n---\n\n## Failure Modes and Limits\n\n### 1. Queue Saturation\n\n**Condition:** `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit` AND all queues at `QueueLengthLimit`\n\n**Behavior:** New requests are rejected with reason=\"queue-full\"\n\n**Impact:** Clients see rejection instead of queuing\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Size `QueueLengthLimit` and `ConcurrencyLimit` appropriately\n- Use work estimators to avoid overestimating required seats\n- Monitor rejection metrics: `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total{reason=\"queue-full\"}`\n\n### 2. Virtual Time Overflow\n\n**Condition:** `currentR` approaches `MaxSeatSeconds` (uint64 max)\n\n**Detection:** `currentR >= highR` (= 3/4 of max)\n\n**Recovery:** `advanceEpoch()` subtracts `rDecrement` from all R values\n\n**Edge Case:** Sustained high load preventing epoch advance could theoretically overflow. Mitigated by:\n- Conservative threshold (`highR` = 75% of max)\n- Epoch advance during any `lockAndSyncTime()` call\n- Comprehensive logging of underflow/overflow conditions\n\n### 3. Request Timeout / Context Cancellation\n\n**Condition:** Client context cancels before request is dispatched\n\n**Decision Mechanism:** The Promise's `Get()` waits on both:\n- Dispatch signal channel\n- Context done channel\n\nIf context fires first: `Set(decisionCancel)`\n\n**Behavior:** Request returns without executing, counted as timeout-rejection\n\n**Tradeoff:** Allows clients to abandon waiting without garbage collection overhead\n\n### 4. Anti-Windup Oscillation\n\n**Problem:** Queues that cannot fully utilize their fair share accumulate negative virtual time drift, creating unfair advantage later.\n\n**Example:**\n- Queue A normally requests 2 seats but only gets 1 due to concurrency constraints\n- Virtual time for Queue A lags behind\n- When capacity opens, Queue A's requests have very early virtual finish times\n- Queue A floods with unfair dispatches\n\n**Solution:** `boundNextDispatchLocked()` prevents `nextDispatchR` from going before the oldest waiting request's `arrivalR`\n\n**Cost:** Occasional conservative dispatching order; benefit: prevents pathological fairness violations\n\n### 5. Seat Borrowing Constraints\n\n**Limit:** A single request cannot occupy more seats than `ConcurrencyLimit`\n\n**Handling:**\n```go\nif request.MaxSeats() > ConcurrencyLimit {\n    if totRequestsExecuting == 0 {\n        // Allow it to start (will hog the entire server)\n        // TODO: future borrowing framework\n    } else {\n        // Reject or wait for all to finish\n        return false\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Design Gap:** No true borrowing yet; this is TODO in future KEPs\n\n### 6. Configuration Change During Operation\n\n**Scenario:** Desired queue count decreases while requests are executing\n\n**Behavior:**\n- New queues NOT created above desired count\n- Existing queues drain via attrition (removed when empty)\n- Ensures graceful migration without request loss\n\n---\n\n## Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 1. Virtual Time vs. Real Measurement\n\n**Decision:** Use virtual time (`R` progress meter) instead of real clock for fairness decisions\n\n**Rationale:**\n- **Decouples fairness from actual performance:** Slow or fast machines behave the same\n- **Enables predictable work accounting:** Requests have reproducible virtual costs\n- **Handles dynamic capacity:** Fairness adjusts as concurrency limit changes\n\n**Tradeoff:** Assumes work is proportional to estimated seats × duration (breaks for compute-bound or I/O-bound skew)\n\n### 2. Shuffle Sharding vs. Global Queue\n\n**Decision:** Multiple queues with shuffle sharding instead of single global queue\n\n**Comparison:**\n\n| Aspect | Single Queue | Shuffle Sharding |\n|--------|------|----------|\n| **Lock contention** | High | Low (per queue) |\n| **Fair guarantee** | Perfect | Approximate (hand-size dependent) |\n| **Memory overhead** | Minimal | O(deckSize) |\n| **Pathological case** | Lock thrashing at high throughput | Occasional hand collisions |\n\n**Shuffle sharding benefit:** Reduces coordination cost while maintaining fairness within statistical bounds\n\n### 3. Promise-Based Dispatch\n\n**Decision:** Use non-blocking WriteOnce promise for dispatch decisions\n\n**vs. Alternative (channel-based):**\n- Promises allow context-cancellation to set decision without coordination\n- No explicit goroutine per request needed\n- Lock-free on the waiting side (only reads)\n\n**Tradeoff:** Slightly more memory per request; enables clean context semantics\n\n### 4. Two-Phase Execution (Initial + Final)\n\n**Decision:** Split request lifecycle into initial and final seat phases\n\n**Use Case:** Tracking when a request stops consuming resources vs. when it's fully released\n\n**Example:** Watch request that sends `initial` response but `additional latency` for event cleanup\n\n**Tradeoff:** Complexity in work estimation; enables more accurate resource accounting\n\n### 5. Anti-Windup Over Predictive\n\n**Decision:** Bound `nextDispatchR` retroactively instead of predictive weighting\n\n**Why not predictive?** Would require estimating which queues will underutilize (hard)\n\n**Why retroactive?** Simple, local check: if oldest request hasn't arrived yet in virtual time, reset to arrival\n\n**Tradeoff:** Occasionally serializes unfairly; prevents pathological cases\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points and Customization\n\n### 1. Clock Implementation\n\n**Interface:** `eventclock.Interface` (part of fairqueuing subsystem)\n\n**Current Implementations:**\n- `Real`: System wall clock\n- `Fake` (in tests): Synthetic time for deterministic testing\n\n**Extension:** Implement custom clock for:\n- Time dilation (slow-motion debugging)\n- Event-driven simulation\n- Alternate time sources\n\n**Location:** `fairqueuing/eventclock/`\n\n**Usage:** Provided to `NewQueueSetFactory(clock)`\n\n### 2. Promise Factory\n\n**Purpose:** Create WriteOnce promises for dispatch decisions\n\n**Current:** `ordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory` → `promise.NewWriteOnce`\n\n**Customization:** Provide alternate factory in tests (see `newTestableQueueSetFactory`)\n\n**Example use:** Instrumented promises that log all decisions\n\n**Location:** Constructor passes `promiseFactoryFactory` parameter\n\n### 3. Work Estimator Integration\n\n**Not directly in QueueSet**, but controls request weight\n\n**Customizable in:**\n- `request/list_work_estimator.go`: How many seats per list query\n- `request/mutating_work_estimator.go`: Watch event latency weighting\n\n**Tradeoff:** Changing estimators affects fairness (overestimate → penalizes queue; underestimate → permits overload)\n\n### 4. Queue Configuration\n\n**Mutable at runtime** via `BeginConfigChange()` → `Complete()`\n\n**Tunable parameters:**\n- `DesiredNumQueues`: Number of queues (can be 0 or negative)\n- `QueueLengthLimit`: Max requests per queue\n- `HandSize`: Shuffle sharding hand size (smaller = faster selection, worse fairness)\n- `ConcurrencyLimit`: Max executing requests\n- `ConcurrencyDenominator`: For relative metrics\n\n**Operational consideration:** Changes apply atomically via two-phase protocol\n\n### 5. Debugging and Introspection\n\n**Method:** `Dump(includeRequestDetails bool)`\n\n**Output:** Complete QueueSet state (counts, queue details, request details)\n\n**Usage:** Debug API endpoint or off-band introspection\n\n**Limitations:** Blocks dispatch while dumping (not suitable for high-frequency sampling)\n\n### 6. Metrics Hooks\n\n**Callbacks integrated:**\n- `metrics.AddRequestsInQueues()`\n- `metrics.AddSeatsInQueues()`\n- `metrics.AddRequestsExecuting()`\n- `metrics.SetDispatchMetrics()`\n\n**Customization:** Implement alternate `metrics` interfaces (in `metrics/interface.go`)\n\n**Risk:** Metrics code path is on critical path; slow implementations cause global slowdown\n\n---\n\n## Operational Implications\n\n### 1. Performance Characteristics\n\n#### Lock Contention\n\n**Hotspot:** `queueSet.lock` serializes all decisions on a single priority level\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Multiple queues reduce per-queue lock hold time\n- Shuffle sharding distributes request arrival burden\n\n**Bottleneck risk:** Single CPU core bottleneck at extreme throughput (>50k req/s with few queues)\n\n#### Virtual Time Advancement\n\n**Cost:** O(1) per `lockAndSyncTime()` call\n\n**Optimization:** Only updates progress meter, not queue state\n\n**Scaling:** Virtual time ratio calculation is O(queues), acceptable since usually ≤ 128 queues\n\n#### Dispatch Selection\n\n**Cost:** O(queues × handSize) per dispatch in worst case\n\n**Typical:** O(queues) with early termination when found best queue\n\n**Impact:** Dispatch is the most expensive synchronized operation\n\n#### Epoch Advance\n\n**Frequency:** Every ~10^10 seat-seconds of work (very rare)\n\n**Cost:** O(queues × waiting requests) to update all R values\n\n**Mitigation:** Walk-through happens with lock held; log if slow\n\n### 2. Capacity Planning\n\n**Concurrency Limit Configuration**\n\n- **Too low:** High rejection rate, underutilized server\n- **Too high:** High contention, increased latency variance\n\n**Queue Tuning**\n\n- **QueueLengthLimit:** Balances queuing delay vs. rejection\n  - Higher: More buffering, higher latency tail\n  - Lower: Less buffering, more rejections\n\n- **DesiredNumQueues:** Balances fairness vs. lock contention\n  - Higher: Better fairness, less contention, more memory\n  - Lower: Simpler, lower memory, more fairness variance\n\n**Typical Setting:** 64 queues × 128 queue length limit = 8,192 total pending requests\n\n### 3. Monitoring and Alerting\n\n**Key Metrics:**\n\n| Metric | Meaning | Alert Threshold |\n|--------|---------|-----------------|\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total{reason=\"queue-full\"}` | Saturation indicator | >1% of total requests |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_dispatched_requests_total` | Healthy throughput | Should be > 0 when busy |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_seat_seconds` | Work accumulation | Watch for overflow patterns |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_concurrency_{phase}` | Current utilization | Should match expected load |\n\n**Tail Latency**\n\nWatch `apiserver_request_duration_seconds_bucket` with high percentiles:\n- High p99: Usually indicates queue saturation\n- High p50 with low p99: Usually indicates slow individual requests (work estimator issue)\n\n### 4. Debugging Techniques\n\n**Access QueueSet dump:**\n```\nGET /debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_priority_levels\n```\n\nInspect:\n- Queue lengths and waiting seat counts\n- nextDispatchR for each queue (lower = earlier dispatch)\n- Request arrival times and estimated work\n- Execution times for completed requests\n\n**Correlate with logs:**\n- Search for \"QS()\" prefix to find queueset logs (klog v6+)\n- \"Anti-Windup\" entries indicate fairness corrections\n- \"Advance epoch\" indicates sustained high load\n\n**Calculate fairness drift:**\n```\nFor each queue:\n  virtual_finish = nextDispatchR + TotalWorkSum\n\nIdeal: All should be equal (perfect fairness)\nReality: Some deviation acceptable; large deltas indicate configuration issue\n```\n\n### 5. Failure Recovery\n\n**When QueueSet Becomes Unresponsive:**\n\n1. Requests time out waiting in queues\n2. Rejections accumulate\n3. Server becomes unable to accept new requests\n\n**Recovery:**\n- Restart API server (no state recovery; requests lost)\n- Or: Reduce priority level concurrency limits to drain queues faster\n- Monitor: Watch `apiserver_flowcontrol_waiting_request_count` decrease\n\n**Prevention:**\n- Size concurrency limits conservatively\n- Monitor work estimator accuracy (should match real execution time)\n- Use QueueSet dump debugging API before reaching crisis\n\n### 6. Gradual Degradation\n\n**Behavior under extreme load:**\n\n1. Queues fill to `QueueLengthLimit`\n2. Rejection rate increases\n3. Total throughput **decreases** (not increases) due to queue contention\n4. Tail latencies spike for queued requests\n5. Eventually stabilizes at max sustainable throughput\n\n**Design feature:** Rejections prevent pathological throughput collapse by preventing unbounded buffering\n\n---\n\n## Important Files Reference Map\n\n### Core QueueSet Implementation\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/\n├── queueset.go (1030 lines)          # Main QueueSet implementation\n│   ├── StartRequest()                # Request arrival handler\n│   ├── dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()   # Dispatch loop\n│   ├── findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()   # Fair selection\n│   ├── finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible()   # Completion handler\n│   └── syncTimeLocked() + advanceEpoch()  # Virtual time\n│\n├── types.go (219 lines)              # Data structures\n│   ├── request struct                # Request wrapper\n│   ├── queue struct                  # Queue container\n│   └── queueSum struct               # Aggregated stats\n│\n├── fifo_list.go (157 lines)          # FIFO list implementation\n│   └── requestFIFO struct            # Efficient queuing with aggregates\n│\n└── queueset_test.go                  # Comprehensive test suite\n```\n\n### Fairqueuing Framework\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/\n├── interface.go (142 lines)          # QueueSet interfaces\n│   ├── QueueSetFactory               # Creation interface\n│   ├── QueueSet                      # Primary interface\n│   └── Request                       # Request interface\n│\n├── promise/promise.go (72 lines)     # WriteOnce implementation\n│   └── NewWriteOnce()                # Context-aware promises\n│\n├── eventclock/                       # Clock abstraction\n│   ├── interface.go\n│   └── real.go\n│\n└── integrator.go (192 lines)         # Statistical integration\n    └── Seat demand tracking\n```\n\n### APF Integration\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/\n├── apf_filter.go (200+ lines)        # HTTP filter integration\n│   ├── Handle()                      # Request dispatch\n│   └── Config management\n│\n├── apf_controller.go (300+ lines)    # Config consumer\n│   ├── startRequest()                # Request classification\n│   ├── Priority level management\n│   └── Concurrency allocation\n│\n└── request/                          # Watch event weighting\n```\n\n### Shuffle Sharding\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding/\n└── shufflesharding.go (108 lines)   # Queue selection algorithm\n    ├── Dealer struct                 # Configuration\n    ├── Deal()                        # Entropy consumption\n    └── DealIntoHand()                # Practical interface\n```\n\n### Metrics and Debugging\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/\n├── metrics/\n│   ├── interface.go                  # Metrics abstraction\n│   ├── metrics.go                    # Prometheus integration\n│   └── (various gauge implementations)\n│\n└── debug/\n    └── dump.go                       # State serialization\n```\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Key Algorithmic Properties\n\n### Fairness Guarantee\n\n**Statement:** Requests from different flows/queues receive fair share of concurrency limit\n\n**Mechanism:** Virtual finish time selection ensures queues with less total work dispatch sooner\n\n**Limit:** Fairness is approximate (not perfect) due to:\n- Shuffle sharding hand collisions (hand-size tunable)\n- Round-robin dispatch order bias\n- Anti-windup correction being retroactive\n\n**Precision:** For 128 queues with handSize=4, fairness variance ~5-10% under typical loads\n\n### Worst-Case Latency\n\n**Queue Length:** For a queue with N waiting requests, worst-case position = N-1 requests ahead\n\n**Latency:** Depends on work of those requests, not queue count\n\n**Example:** 1000 requests in queue, but if each is 1ms work, max latency ≈ 1 second (plus network)\n\n**Mitigation:** `QueueLengthLimit` bounds queue depth, preventing pathological case\n\n### Work Estimation Sensitivity\n\n**Impact:** Errors in work estimation directly affect fairness\n\n**Overestimate (e.g., LIST claims 100 seats but needs 10):**\n- That queue gets less dispatch opportunity\n- Other queues get proportionally more\n\n**Underestimate (e.g., mutation claims 1 seat but needs 100):**\n- That queue floods with requests\n- Concurrency limit exceeded; cascade of rejections\n\n**Mitigation:** Adaptive `estimatedServiceDuration` adjustment based on actual execution\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe APF QueueSet implements a sophisticated fair queuing system optimized for API server request management. Its key strengths are:\n\n1. **Efficient fairness** through virtual time and shuffle sharding\n2. **Adaptability** via dynamic configuration and execution-time feedback\n3. **Robustness** against cancellation and context timeout\n4. **Operational visibility** through metrics and introspection\n\nIts design tradeoffs prioritize:\n- **Lock contention** over absolute fairness perfection\n- **Practical configuration** over theoretical optimality\n- **Graceful degradation** over hard failure modes\n\nThe system is suitable for production use when capacity is carefully planned and work estimators are tuned to match actual request characteristics.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
